{"nick":"joepie91","message":"jjrabbit: whether the operation succeeded or failed is encoded in the Promise itself (whether it's \"resolved\"/successful or \"rejected\"/failed); if it's resolved, then it contains a value (like a number, or an object, or whatever the result of the operation is) and if it's rejected, then it contains an Error object of some sort","date":"2018-09-06T15:59:50.131Z","type":"message"}
{"nick":"joepie91","message":"(an Error object like what you might `throw`)","date":"2018-09-06T15:59:59.120Z","type":"message"}
{"nick":"joepie91","message":"you specify different behaviour for the resolved vs. rejected cases","date":"2018-09-06T16:00:14.469Z","type":"message"}
{"nick":"joepie91","message":".then only defines the behaviour for a resolved case, ie. when the operation succeeded","date":"2018-09-06T16:00:24.851Z","type":"message"}

{"nick":"joepie91","message":"the promise containing a 'result' only happens when it succeeds/resolves","date":"2018-09-06T16:01:02.883Z","type":"message"}
